# GSD-T Progress

## Project: GSD-T Framework (@tekyzinc/gsd-t)
## Status: ACTIVE — **M99 COMPLETED 2026-06-30 (v4.14.10) — Graph Observability & Consolidation.** All graph artifacts consolidated under `.gsd-t/graphDB/` via a copy-verify-swap migration shim (WAL-checkpoint before copy, idempotent, interruption-safe, never-orphan); the graph-vs-grep DECISION is now observable through a toggleable, rotated, fail-open telemetry ledger (every graph query + grep-intercept + read-intercept decision + each workflow's WIRED/fallback/disabled mode) surfaced via `gsd-t graph metrics` (hit-vs-passthrough ratio, fallback-rate, p50/p95 latency, tier mix, per-consumer/verb, `fallbackAnnouncedDespiteHit` north-star). 3 domains / 2 waves. The orthogonal-triad verify caught + FIXED **3 real HIGH bugs** (migration WAL data-loss on interruption 4000→2000; rollup prototype-pollution crash; SCIP files outside graphDB — SC#1 falsified) + a casing bug (scan "wired" vs rollup "WIRED"), all with regression tests. Suite green (2600+). Archived to `.gsd-t/milestones/m99-graph-observability-2026-06-30/`. NEXT: `/cpua` publish + propagate, then scan #47. PRIOR: **M98 FOLLOW-UP FIX 2026-06-29 (v4.13.11): `gsd-t graph body` was unreachable from the front door — the M98 `body` slice logic lived in the query CLI + Read-intercept hook, but the top-level `gsd-t graph` router in `bin/gsd-t.js` had no `case "body"`, so `gsd-t graph body <fn>` fell through to "Unknown graph subcommand". Found by checking real binvoice. Fix: 1 router case + usage string + a front-door regression test (M98's test only exercised the CLI directly). Verified on binvoice: front-door `graph body selectCommentId` now returns the live 43-line slice. Suite 2541/2545. PRIOR: M98 SHIPPED 2026-06-29 (v4.13.10) — The Graph Serves Code. The code graph now serves function-level source SLICES, not just an index: `gsd-t graph body <funcId|symbol>` reads the live file, slices start..end (new `nodes.end_line` column), attaches imports + class header + callers; ambiguous symbol → candidates; a PostToolUse `Read`-intercept hook augments a structural read with a pointer to the precise slice (default pass-through, never shrinks; fail-open). Proven on real binvoice: 43-line fn from a 1,334-line file = 21× fewer chars. Red Team found+FIXED 3 bugs (tier-downgrade, output-truncation, db-leak). Suite 2540/2540. Graph arc: M94 index → M95 SCIP → M96 runs-in-projects → M97 grep-intercept → M98 serve-code. NEXT: `/cpua` publish+propagate.** PRIOR GRAPH ARC: M97 (v4.12.10) grep-intercept + Python call-graphs · M96 (v4.10.11) graph runs in projects · M95 real SCIP resolution · M94 (DEFINED→built) persistent index. PRIOR: **M93 COMPLETED 2026-06-23 (v4.9.11) — Brevity Guard. Conciseness is now ENFORCED, not requested: a BLOCKING `Stop` hook (`scripts/gsd-t-brevity-guard.js`, wired LIVE into `~/.claude/settings.json`) catches answer-mode preamble/process-narration + bare unglossed jargon before the user reads it (action-mode intent-first stays allowed; FAIL-OPEN so it never gags legit work) + a Reader Contract in CLAUDE-global/subagent-prompts (the default) + `bin/gsd-t-jargon-lint.cjs` (flag unglossed jargon in docs). Root cause: the user asked for conciseness for weeks; prose rules get ignored (even my own "no process narration"); GSD-T only obeys deterministic GATES. 3 file-disjoint domains / 1 wave. VERIFIED-WITH-WARNINGS: QA PASS (47/47, 4 mutations caught incl fail-open); Red Team GRUDGING-PASS (opus) — exhaustively attacked fail-open, HELD; 2 findings fixed in-verify + a detector gap caught at integrate. ## Current Milestone

### M99 — Graph Observability & Consolidation — **DEFINED 2026-06-30 07:48 PDT (awaiting partition)**

**Status: DEFINED.** Origin/goal/falsifiable-acceptance authored; partition/plan DEFERRED (DEFINE-only). Competition selected the **RISK-FIRST** proposal (winner B of 3). Two-altitude intention-first docs authored: [`PseudoCode-GraphObservability.md`](pseudocode/PseudoCode-GraphObservability.md) (telemetry layers) + [`PseudoCode-GraphFolderMigration.md`](pseudocode/PseudoCode-GraphFolderMigration.md) (path migration). Event + rollup schema: [`graph-metrics-contract.md`](contracts/graph-metrics-contract.md). Full definition below.

**The one-breath call:** move every graph artifact under one folder (`.gsd-t/graphDB/`, existing graphs auto-migrated so nothing is orphaned), then make the graph-vs-grep DECISION VISIBLE — one append-only telemetry ledger records, for every graph query, every grep interception, and every read interception, whether the graph was consulted and whether it answered or fell back to grep — surfaced through a `gsd-t graph metrics` rollup (hit-vs-fallback ratio, latency, tier mix, per-consumer/per-verb). Telemetry is toggleable and rotates by size/count.

**RISK-FIRST sequencing (the signed-off decision):** the scope is locked; the SEQUENCING is the lever. Front-load the riskiest, hardest-to-reverse work so failure is cheap and early. **Tier 0** = the migration shim (HIGHEST risk: the only irreversible, data-touching step — Destructive Action Guard applies; copy-verify-swap, never orphan; prove in isolation BEFORE any path-literal change). **Tier 1** = path consolidation behind ONE resolver (HIGH risk: ~7 scattered literals + 20 test files; a missed literal = M96-class silent split-brain). **Tier 2** = Layer-2 decision logging (the REASON the milestone exists; fail-open invariant is the proof obligation). **Tier 3** = Layer-1 fold-in + rotation + toggle (mostly relocation). **Tier 4** = the read-side rollup CLI + contract (LOWEST risk; last).

> **Two-altitude sign-off (M87, default-ON — logged, not skipped).** The Altitude-1 high-level approach (the one-breath call + risk-first tiers above) is the sign-off checkpoint between altitudes. In this finalizer pass the approach is recorded AND the Altitude-2 detailed docs were authored (above) so the milestone source-of-truth exists before partition; **no skip taken** (`feedback_no_silent_degradation`). Keep-or-supersede over the ONE inherited model (uncommitted Layer-1 ledger): the sink-path move (`metrics/` → `graphDB/logs/`) + added rotation/toggle is an explicit SUPERSEDE → `⚠ Divergence` flags written in both docs; the Layer-1 record SHAPE, the FAIL-OPEN invariant, the read-intercept never-shrink rule, and the `GSDT_GRAPH_CONSUMER` convention are KEPT (no flag).

**Falsifiable acceptance (16 criteria — full list in the definition below):** consolidation+migration (1–5: all artifacts under `graphDB/`, auto-migrate identical-answer, idempotent+interruption-safe, zero raw literals, 20 tests pass) · Layer-1 fold-in (6–8: sink at `graphDB/logs/`, sized rotation, on/off flag) · Layer-2 decision logging (9–13: one line per grep / per read / byte-identical on-off / consumer labels / wiring-mode persisted+stamped — the NiceNote north-star) · Layer-3 rollup (14–15: `gsd-t graph metrics` + `graph-metrics-contract.md`) · integration (16: full suite + triad, Red Team probes the destructive path + fail-open).

**Next:** `/gsd-t-partition` (Wave 1 = Tier 0 migration shim + Tier 1 resolver, file-disjoint, gated before any telemetry work).

## M99 — Graph Observability & Consolidation — DEFINITION (DEFINED 2026-06-30 07:48 PDT)

**Competition outcome:** winner B of 3 (the RISK-FIRST proposal). Salvaged non-conflicting line-items: from Candidate A — the "D1 is the minimum lovable increment" framing (Tier 3 fold-in is usable telemetry on its own). From Candidate C — the **projectRoot-derivation hazard** (verified: `bin/gsd-t-graph-query-cli.cjs:515` + the Layer-1 logger root at `:1246` both compute `path.dirname(path.dirname(storePath))`, assuming `.gsd-t/graph.db` is 2 levels above root; moving one directory deeper breaks the derivation → sink/freshness/rollup silently target the wrong tree). Folded into Tier 1 as `[RULE] projectroot-depth-corrected-with-move` (atomic with the path move). NO file ownership assigned at define time (partition deferred).

### Origin
- **Manual graph-telemetry archaeology this session.** Decision-log `2026-06-30 06:34 PDT (v4.13.12)`: a real NiceNote scan #12 announced `GRAPH-FALLBACK — graph index not available` and ran grep-mode while the graph was demonstrably LIVE (156 files, compiler-accurate, all verbs + freshness verified that same session). The fallback was invisible because NOTHING recorded the graph-vs-grep decision.
- **Memory pointers:** `project_code_graph_universal_consumer`, `feedback_graph_is_architectural_anchor` (graph observability is peer-priority to contracts), `project_scan_findings_enrich_graph` + `project_flaky_test_telemetry_gap` (graph as shared observability infra).
- **Layer 1 already built + uncommitted** in the working tree: `bin/gsd-t-graph-query-cli.cjs` modified (adds `_logGraphEvent` appending to `.gsd-t/metrics/graph-events.jsonl`), `test/m99-graph-telemetry.test.js` new, `.gitignore` modified — confirmed via `git status` this session.

### GOAL
One consolidated graph folder (`.gsd-t/graphDB/`) with zero orphaned legacy graphs, and a single append-only telemetry ledger that makes the graph-vs-grep decision observable at every interception point — surfaced through `gsd-t graph metrics`. After this milestone, "did the graph answer, or did we silently fall back to grep, and what for?" is answerable from telemetry, not archaeology.

### CENTRAL TENET ALIGNMENT
The graph is GSD-T's MANDATORY structural-knowledge layer (the M94 CENTRAL TENET, peer-priority to contracts). Its observability must be peer-priority too: a layer you cannot see firing cannot be trusted. M99 is the OBSERVABILITY substrate the next graph consumers (scan-WRITES-graph, flaky-test-telemetry) build on — named OUT of scope here for traceability, sequenced after.

### SUCCESS CRITERIA (falsifiable acceptance)

**Folder consolidation + migration (Tier 0/1):**
1. After `gsd-t graph build`, ALL of `graph.db`, `graph.db-wal`, `graph.db-shm`, `index.scip`, `index-python.scip`, and `logs/` live under `.gsd-t/graphDB/`. FALSIFIER: any written outside `.gsd-t/graphDB/` after a clean build → FAIL.
2. A project with a pre-existing `.gsd-t/graph.db` (+scip) is auto-migrated into `.gsd-t/graphDB/`; the migrated graph answers `gsd-t graph` queries identically to pre-migration. **TRIGGER (user-locked):** the migration fires automatically during **CPUA propagation** — `gsd-t update-all` runs the shim in each registered project — AND as a self-heal safety net on a project's first graph touch if it somehow wasn't propagated. One-shot, idempotent. **WAL-safety (claims-pipeline TODO #1):** before moving, the shim CHECKPOINTs the SQLite write-ahead log (or moves `graph.db` + `-wal` + `-shm` together) so no uncommitted change is left in an orphaned sidecar. FALSIFIER: post-migration query returns `graph-unavailable`, a different result set than a control copy, or loses `-wal`-pending changes → FAIL.
3. The shim is idempotent (second run = no-op) AND interruption-safe (kill mid-migration → a readable graph remains, old or new, never neither). FALSIFIER: re-run errors, or an interrupted run leaves zero readable graph → FAIL.
4. `grep -rn "\.gsd-t/graph\.db|'graph\.db'" bin/ scripts/` returns ZERO raw literals outside the single resolver helper + the migration shim. FALSIFIER: any surviving raw literal in a reader/writer → FAIL (the M96 split-brain guard).
5. All ~20 hardcoded-path tests pass against the new layout (updated or routed through the resolver). **Test-fixture safety (claims-pipeline TODO #3):** the migration shim only ever runs in a REAL project root, never in a test's throwaway `mkdtemp` dir — so a fixture that builds a graph at the old path cannot be relocated mid-test. LOW stakes (test-hygiene, not user data), but the plan confirms no fixture+shim co-location. FALSIFIER: any graph test still asserting `.gsd-t/graph.db` as the live path, or a fixture the shim could relocate → FAIL.

**Telemetry — Layer 1 fold-in (Tier 3):**
6. Layer-1 sink is `.gsd-t/graphDB/logs/graph-events-NNN.jsonl` (NOT `.gsd-t/metrics/`); each query still records verb/target/outcome(hit|hit-empty|ambiguous|not-found|graph-unavailable)/tier/resultCount/latencyMs/consumer/via + freshness staleOnQuery/reindexedCount/reindexedFiles. FALSIFIER: any event written to the old `.gsd-t/metrics/graph-events.jsonl` path → FAIL.
7. Rotation caps by FILE SIZE or ENTRY-COUNT, NOT daily; rollover produces `-001` → `-002` → …. The cap is sized HIGH (≈ **50 MB or 250,000 entries**) so a full on-flag ANALYSIS SESSION lands in ONE file — the cap is a runaway BACKSTOP, not routine rotation (the ledger is an on-demand analysis artifact I read whole, so mid-session splitting hurts analysis). FALSIFIER: a single unbounded file, daily rotation, or a cap so low a normal session splits → FAIL. (Concrete number confirmed against measured heavy-session growth at plan time — claims-pipeline TODO #2, RESOLVED to the 50 MB / 250k target here.)
8. Telemetry is toggleable via an explicit flag; OFF writes zero ledger lines and the graph still answers normally. **POSTURE (user-locked):** the ledger is an ON-DEMAND ANALYSIS artifact (flip on → do heavy work → flip off → I analyze how the graph is used and optimize), NOT an always-on live monitor — that overhead isn't worth it when things work. Live break-detection stays the job of the existing `GRAPH-FALLBACK reason=… via=…` log line (fires in-the-moment regardless of the telemetry flag). FALSIFIER: toggle absent, OFF still appends, or the design couples telemetry to break-detection → FAIL.

**Telemetry — Layer 2 decision logging (Tier 2):**
9. The grep-intercept hook appends ONE ledger line per decision: `{kind:"grep", classified:"structural"|"text", action:"replaced"|"passthrough", patternShape, consumer}`. EVERY grep is logged (tokens=0, disk append, sub-ms). FALSIFIER: a grep interception with no ledger line → FAIL.
10. The read-intercept hook appends ONE line per augment-vs-passthrough decision. FALSIFIER: a read interception with no ledger line → FAIL.
11. The classify→replace/passthrough and augment/passthrough decisions are BYTE-IDENTICAL with telemetry on vs. off (logging never alters fail-open passthrough). FALSIFIER: any decision divergence between on/off → FAIL.
12. Each of the 6 consumers (scan/verify/debug/integrate/quick/phase) + 2 hooks sets `GSDT_GRAPH_CONSUMER`, and the ledger attributes usage to the correct consumer label. FALSIFIER: a consumer's events labeled `cli`/unknown → FAIL.
13. Each workflow's `graphWiringMode` (WIRED|fallback-announced|disabled) is persisted into the ledger AND stamped into the scan report header. FALSIFIER: the NiceNote-class invisible fallback (announced fallback with a live graph) leaves no `graphWiringMode` trace in the ledger → FAIL. **(This is the milestone's north-star test.)**

**Telemetry — Layer 3 rollup (Tier 4):**
14. `gsd-t graph metrics` exists, mirrors `gsd-t metrics` shape, and reports: graph-hit-vs-grep-passthrough ratio, fallback-rate, p50/p95 latency, tier mix, stale-query frequency, reindex frequency, per-consumer + per-verb breakdown. FALSIFIER: any dimension missing, or it crashes on an empty/rotated ledger → FAIL.
15. A `graph-metrics-contract.md` documents the ledger event schema + the rollup output shape. FALSIFIER: contract absent or out of sync with the emitted event keys → FAIL.

**Integration:**
16. Full suite green including `test/m99-graph-telemetry.test.js` (folded in) + new migration/rotation/decision-logging tests (heavy graph tests via `--test-concurrency=1 GSDT_SLOW_TESTS=1`). The orthogonal triad (code-review ultra + Red Team + QA) passes; Red Team specifically probes the migration's destructive path and the fail-open invariant.

### SCOPE BOUNDARY (locked — do NOT re-litigate)
IN: items 1–16 (folder reorg + migration shim + Layers 1/2/3 + rotation + on/off flag). OUT (deferred backlog, named for traceability): scan-findings-enrich-graph (scan WRITES graph), flaky-test-telemetry (graph as shared observability infra) — the NEXT consumers of this observability substrate, not part of M99. Also OUT: changing graph query semantics, tiers, or the M98 body-slice behavior (pure observability + relocation).

### DESTRUCTIVE ACTION GUARD
The folder consolidation is a PATH MIGRATION relocating a real project's `graph.db`. Per the Guard, the user-approved locked decision is: copy-then-verify-then-swap with the old graph retained until the new one is proven readable; the shim NEVER deletes the only readable graph. This is the explicit approval recorded in the locked scope — no further re-litigation; the shim's interruption-safety (criterion 3) is the proof obligation.

### GSD-T-NATIVE EFFORT
- **Domain count:** ~4 (migration+resolver | Layer-2 hooks+wiring | Layer-1 fold-in+rotation+sink | Layer-3 rollup+contract) — medium.
- **Wave count:** risk-first ordering → Tier 0/1 first (gate), then Tier 2/3 (file-disjoint, parallel), then Tier 4.
- **Parallel-domain count:** 2 once Tier 0/1 land (Layer-2 hooks vs Layer-1 CLI are file-disjoint).
- **Token-spend range:** defer precise $ to plan (comparable: M94–M98 graph milestones in `.gsd-t/token-log.md`).

### M94 — Persistent Code Graph Index (Phase 1, backlog #44b graph half) — **DEFINED 2026-06-25 12:48 PDT (awaiting partition)**

**Status: DEFINED.** Origin/goal/falsifiable-acceptance authored; partition/plan DEFERRED (this is a DEFINE-only milestone). UN-gated — M92 (#44a) shipped at v4.9.10, which was the gate on this graph half. Competition selected the **RISK-FIRST** proposal (winner B of 3). Detailed intention-first behavior map authored: [`.gsd-t/pseudocode/PseudoCode-CodeGraphIndex.md`](.gsd-t/pseudocode/PseudoCode-CodeGraphIndex.md) (two-altitude flow — see the sign-off note in the definition below). Full definition follows.

**The one-breath call:** build a codebase's structure ONCE into a persistent, all-local, no-paid-license, on-disk index (files, functions, imports/exports, import graph file→file, call graph function→function) — parsed by **tree-sitter as the always-bundled floor**, upgraded to compiler-accurate **SCIP** per-language where a local indexer is present — kept fresh by **per-file content-hash dirty-detection** (re-index the touched file + re-check its one-hop edges on query) — queried by a **deterministic CLI the model cannot route around** (fresh-or-reindex-inline, never a grep fallback, FAIL-LOUD on parser death) — and wire **`/scan` first** so run-2 reads-once-queries-after instead of re-reading the whole Atos repo every run.

**RISK-FIRST wave shape (the signed-off decision):** the two existential unknowns the research left genuinely OPEN — the embedded store choice (K1) and whether tree-sitter can index Atos in budget (K2) — are **Wave-1 PROVE-OR-KILL spikes** with hard numeric kill-criteria, measured on the REAL Atos repo, BEFORE any indexer / freshness / query-CLI / `/scan`-wiring work begins. A fatal "can't hold the invariant / can't hit the budget" failure then costs one spike-wave, not a built-and-wired milestone.

> **Two-altitude sign-off (M87, default-ON — logged, not skipped).** The Altitude-1 high-level approach (above + in the definition) is the sign-off checkpoint between altitudes. In this finalizer pass the approach is recorded AND the Altitude-2 detailed doc was authored ([`PseudoCode-CodeGraphIndex.md`](.gsd-t/pseudocode/PseudoCode-CodeGraphIndex.md)) so the milestone source-of-truth exists before partition; **no skip taken** (`feedback_no_silent_degradation`). The keep-or-supersede ledger over the inherited M20–M21 models is applied in §Divergence of that doc (3 supersedes → 3 `⚠ Divergence` flags; the edge-taxonomy WHAT is KEPT, no flag).

**Falsifiable acceptance — sequenced into waves (full criteria in the definition below):**
- **Wave 1 (PROVE-OR-KILL):** K1 store-bakeoff (embedded/no-server/no-paid + query-latency + sub-~1s incremental, else re-scope) · K2 tree-sitter Atos full index under ~2 min (AC-1, else re-scope). HARD gate.
- **Wave 2 (BUILD):** AC-2 who-imports/who-calls correctness (hand-checked fixtures) · AC-3 incremental freshness sub-~1s with the uncommitted-edit killing test · AC-5 no-stale-no-wrong invariant (structural grep-for-absence of any grep fallback + fault-injection fail-loud) · AC-6 honest accuracy tiers (SCIP compiler-accurate / tree-sitter floor labeled / Rust cross-crate flagged-partial).
- **Wave 3 (WIRE):** AC-4 `/scan` INSIGHT delta — graph-wired scan surfaces ≥ the no-graph run + ≥1 missed/wrong structural finding (pinned Atos SHA). Scan kept intact; speed/file-count deferred to a separate scan-redesign milestone.

**Next:** `/gsd-t-partition` (Wave 1 = D1 store-spike ∥ tree-sitter-spike, prove-or-kill; defer the milestone body to Waves 2–3).

---

## M94 — Persistent Code Graph Index (Phase 1, backlog #44b graph half) — DEFINITION (DEFINED 2026-06-25 12:48 PDT)

**Competition outcome:** winner B of 3 (the RISK-FIRST proposal). Salvaged non-conflicting line-items from A (FASTEST-TIME-TO-VALUE) + C (DEPENDENCY-ORDER): C's per-criterion "which layer this validates" framing reinforces the wave pinning; A's "thin vertical slice" framing is consistent with the narrow `/scan`-first consumer set. No file ownership assigned at define time (partition deferred).

### Origin
- **Backlog #44b** — the graph half of the Understand-Before-Build pipeline fix. Sibling **#44a** (the no-graph paradigm half) shipped as **M92 (v4.9.10)**; the gate on #44b is now lifted.
- **Direct evidence:** the BinVoice 2026-06-22 four-failure session — wrong-altitude plans that grep-grounding (M92) gets ~80% of, but the "starve-the-source" and N≥3-consolidation cases are relationship questions grep structurally can't answer.
- **The decisive reframe (this session):** full-index-up-front beats build-on-demand because on-demand can't catch the unknown-unknown dependency and can't speed up `/scan`. This INVERTS the design-brief's earlier "build-on-demand, store nothing" decision — see Divergence in [`PseudoCode-CodeGraphIndex.md`](.gsd-t/pseudocode/PseudoCode-CodeGraphIndex.md).
- **Prior-art autopsy (read this session):** GSD-T shipped a full code graph in **M20–M21 (v2.38–2.39)** and it DIED. The 6 `bin/graph-*.js` files are still in the tree; `gsd-t graph status` today returns "No graph index found" (verified this session). Cause of death inverted point-by-point below.

### CENTRAL TENET (the spine of the whole build — user directive 2026-06-25)
**Dumb reach vs. smart reach into code (the user's framing).** DUMB reach = today: the LLM gets a pile of text and must assemble + figure out the structure before it can reason. SMART reach = the graph: relationships are already organized and identified, so the LLM does the one thing only it can do — **think — with all the facts already in hand.** The code graph is the MANDATORY structural-knowledge layer for every workflow step that reaches into code (for structure, downstream effects, or debugging); no code-reading step reconstructs from raw text what the graph already knows. This is the governing architecture, not a feature of one command. Every code-reading consumer (`/scan`, `/debug`, `/quick`, `/execute` file-disjointness, `/impact`, `/plan`, partition, M92's simplicity reflex) is designed to consume the graph BY DEFAULT and gains the same four wins: (1) fewer tokens (compact graph ≪ raw source); (2) skip relationship-tracing (call chains / imports / dependents / dead-code / cycles PRE-COMPUTED, not reconstructed by reading); (3) pre-organized for reasoning — the LLM skips comprehension and goes straight to judgment (less reasoning load = faster AND better); (4) better/accurate structural insight. Only deep logic-bug reading inside a function is not graph-replaceable (but the LLM arrives oriented). **Scope discipline (avoids the M20–M21 "21-commands-at-once" death): the tenet is the PRINCIPLE + the shared query layer + the contract MANDATE that code-reading steps consume the graph; Phase 1 WIRES `/scan` + the query CLI as the first proof; the other consumers are MANDATED, SEQUENCED follow-ons — in-scope by principle, sequenced by execution, never dropped.**

### Goal
A persistent, all-LOCAL (no network, no API, no paid license), embedded on-disk index of codebase structure — files, functions, imports/exports, an import graph (file→file) and a call graph (function→function) — built once up-front, kept fresh by content-hash incremental re-indexing, and queried by a deterministic CLI the model cannot route around, serving as the central structural-knowledge layer per the tenet above. **`/scan` is wired first as the falsifiable PROOF of the tenet** (faster AND better-insight, both measured), not the goal in itself. `gsd-t graph status` returning a live queryable index on the Atos repo is the success state; the M20–M21 "no index found" is the anti-goal.

### Locked architecture (settled with the user — NOT re-litigated)
- **Parser floor:** tree-sitter (always bundled; parses TS/JS, Python, Rust, any language; syntax-level edges; works with nothing else installed). Distinct from the ARCHIVED tree-sitter-stack-graphs RESOLVER — explicitly NOT used.
- **Resolver upgrade:** SCIP per-language indexers — scip-typescript, scip-python, rust-analyzer `scip`. Free (Apache-2.0/MIT), one-shot LOCAL CLIs, emit `index.scip`. Present → that language upgraded to compiler-accurate; absent → tree-sitter floor (approximate). **The graph NEVER depends on an external tool to FUNCTION — only to get BETTER.**
- **Languages:** TS/JS full accuracy, Python full accuracy, **Rust BEST-EFFORT** (rust-analyzer SCIP officially "limited"; within-crate resolves, cross-crate partial → must be FLAGGED partial, never silently wrong).
- **Storage:** embedded, on-disk, NO server, NO paid license (Glean-style embedded KV, not a graph-DB server). **The SPECIFIC store is DEFERRED to the K1 plan/Wave-1 spike** — an OPEN decision, NOT picked here.
- **Freshness:** per-file CONTENT-HASH dirty-detection (not git-SHA — must catch uncommitted working-tree edits). On query: hash touched files vs stored; stale → re-index that file + re-validate ONE-HOP edges (NOT transitive). Sub-second per edit. Query is a DETERMINISTIC CLI: fresh-or-reindexes-inline; the model NEVER chooses grep-fallback; never serve a stale OR wrong edge; parser genuinely can't load → FAIL LOUD (graph-unavailable, commands run in grep mode).

### How M94 INVERTS every documented M20–M21 cause of death
| M20–M21 died of | M94 inverts it |
|---|---|
| Persistent index synced every command boundary → staleness + sync-firefighting | Content-hash incremental, lazy on query — only touched files re-hashed, only their one-hop edges re-checked; sub-second; no eager whole-repo sync. |
| External Neo4j / Docker / CGC / Python infra → Windows bugs, encoding crashes, auto-setup backlog | Embedded local store (no server) + FREE local SCIP indexers (no network, no daemon). SCIP absence degrades to tree-sitter floor, never breaks. |
| Always-on, wired into 21 commands, value diffuse | Narrow consumer set, `/scan` FIRST (one falsifiable win: ~2hr → fast run-2). Others added incrementally, each justified. |
| Built-first, justified-later (comparison written AFTER shipping found it marginal) | Falsifiable metrics up-front + gated on M92 (SHIPPED). AND risk-first: the two existential metrics are Wave-1 kill-criteria measured on the REAL Atos repo before the body is built. |
| Regex parsers that "logged their own parser bugs" | tree-sitter floor replaces regex. `bin/graph-parsers.js` read for LESSONS only (which edges to extract) — NOT lifted. Build fresh. |
| Silent grep fallthrough across 21 commands (the VERIFIED root cause) | No directive-driven grep fallback at all. Deterministic CLI; parser death = FAIL-LOUD graph-unavailable, never a silent half-accurate index. |

### Keep-or-Supersede ledger (inherited M20–M21 models — applied; see [`PseudoCode-CodeGraphIndex.md`](.gsd-t/pseudocode/PseudoCode-CodeGraphIndex.md) §Divergence)
Per `templates/prompts/keep-or-supersede-subagent.md`, each inherited model got an explicit keep/supersede decision; each supersede WROTE a `⚠ Divergence` flag:
1. **"Store nothing — build-on-demand per planning step"** → **SUPERSEDE** (persistent full-index-up-front; on-demand can't catch unknown dependencies or speed `/scan`). Flag written.
2. **"3-tier provider chain CGC→native→grep with silent model-chosen grep fallthrough"** → **SUPERSEDE** (tree-sitter floor + optional SCIP upgrade, NO grep fallback, FAIL-LOUD on parser death). Flag written.
3. **"Entity/edge extraction set" (regex parsers)** → **KEEP the WHAT (which edges), SUPERSEDE the HOW (regex→tree-sitter)**. Flag on the HOW only.

### Falsifiable Success Criteria (the six, sequenced RISK-FIRST into waves)
**WAVE 1 — PROVE-OR-KILL (the two existential unknowns; NO milestone-body build until both pass):**
- **K1 (store bakeoff — KILL CRITERION).** Spike the DEFERRED store options (KuzuDB embedded-Cypher / SQLite recursive-CTE / JSONL / graphology) against a SYNTHETIC ~1.5M-node graph (Atos scale). **PASS iff** one option is (a) embedded/on-disk/no-server/no-paid-license, (b) answers "who imports X" + "who calls f" within the query-latency target, AND (c) supports a single-file incremental update + one-hop edge re-validation in **under ~1s**. NO option clears all three → **KILL/re-scope** (e.g., narrow Phase-1 to import-graph-only, or cap repo size). Store PICKED here on evidence.
- **K2 (tree-sitter Atos throughput — KILL CRITERION = AC-1).** Run the tree-sitter floor over the REAL Atos repo (~1.5M LOC, mostly TS + some Python). **PASS iff** full index builds in **under ~2 min**. Can't → **KILL/re-scope** budget/parallelism before building on a false premise.

**WAVE 2 — BUILD (only after K1+K2 pass):**
- **AC-2 (who-imports/who-calls correctness).** "Who imports X" returns the correct DIRECT importers (hand-checked Atos fixtures); "who calls f" returns correct direct callers.
- **AC-3 (incremental freshness).** Editing a file marks it stale (content-hash mismatch) and re-indexes it + re-checks its one-hop edges in **under ~1s**. Killing test: an uncommitted working-tree edit (git-SHA unchanged) IS caught.
- **AC-5 (no-stale-no-wrong invariant — keystone).** (a) no directive-driven grep fallback in any code path (structural grep-for-absence); (b) parser-load failure → LOUD graph-unavailable, verified by fault-injection (force a parser to fail → assert CLI returns graph-unavailable, never a partial edge).
- **AC-6 (accuracy tiers honest).** TS/Python compiler-accurate where SCIP present; tree-sitter floor (approximate, LABELED) where absent; Rust cross-crate FLAGGED partial. Killing test: a known Rust cross-crate edge returns tagged `partial`, and the same repo with scip-typescript present returns a TS edge tagged `compiler-accurate`.

**WAVE 3 — CONSUMER WIRING (the falsifiable payoff — PROOF of the tenet via INSIGHT; `/scan` kept fully intact):**
- **AC-4 (`/scan` smart-reach — headline = INSIGHT delta, NOT speed/file-count).** SCOPE DECISION (user, 2026-06-25): M94 keeps the CURRENT `/scan` architecture **fully intact** (it works, it's praised — do not disrupt). The graph is wired ADDITIVELY: its pre-computed structural findings (dependents, dead-code, cycles, coupling) are injected into `/scan` so those findings are accurate, not LLM-reconstructed. **Falsifiable proof = INSIGHT, measured on a pinned Atos SHA (neither asserted):** a graph-wired `/scan` surfaces ≥ the no-graph run's structural findings PLUS ≥1 the no-graph run MISSED or got WRONG (a real dead-code / cycle / dependent the raw-read reconstruction failed to catch). **The "reads fewer files / faster" claim is DROPPED from M94** — it cannot bind without redesigning scan's enumerate-EVERY-file logic-bug mandate (finding in-file logic defects genuinely requires reading the file; a relationship graph holds no logic). That redesign is a SEPARATE future milestone ("re-think `/scan` from the graph up" — [[feedback_nothing_in_gsdt_is_concrete]]), NOT M94. AC-4 proves the tenet where it HONESTLY binds (insight / accuracy / determinism), not where it can't (file-read speed without a scan redesign).

### Explicitly OUT OF SCOPE (Phase 1)
- **Docs-in-graph** — Phase 2 (doc↔doc + item↔item + doc-item↔code edges via DECLARED IDs only like `@implements R-12`, never prose inference).
- **N≥3 consolidation lens** beyond what blast-radius gives.
- **Consumers beyond `/scan`** — `/impact`, `/debug`, `/quick`, `/execute` file-disjointness, M92's simplicity reflex are MANDATED, SEQUENCED follow-on wiring per the Central Tenet (in-scope by principle, sequenced by execution — NOT dropped); only `/scan` is WIRED in Phase 1 as the first proof. The shared query layer + the contract mandate that code-reading steps consume the graph are Phase-1 deliverables so the follow-ons are wiring, not redesign.

### Acceptance (milestone COMPLETE iff)
1. K1 + K2 passed in Wave 1, store PICKED on evidence, both metrics recorded in progress.md.
2. AC-2/3/5/6 pass with their killing tests green (real Atos fixtures, fault-injection for AC-5).
3. AC-4 measured (INSIGHT proof only — `/scan` kept intact): graph-wired `/scan` structural-insight ≥ the no-graph run PLUS ≥1 finding the no-graph run missed/got wrong, on a pinned Atos SHA, in progress.md + CHANGELOG. Speed/file-count is OUT of M94 (deferred to the separate scan-redesign milestone).
4. `gsd-t graph status` returns a live, queryable index on the Atos repo (the M20–M21 "no index found" state is the anti-goal).
5. No grep-fallback code path exists (structural grep proof); parser-death FAIL-LOUD verified by injection.
6. [`PseudoCode-CodeGraphIndex.md`](.gsd-t/pseudocode/PseudoCode-CodeGraphIndex.md) authored (done at define time), keep-or-supersede ledger applied with Divergence flags, guard-map `[RULE]` set feeds the verify gate.

### Pre-Partition Assessment (GSD-T-native units — NO human-time)
- **Domain count:** ~4–5 (medium-complex): D1 store-spike + tree-sitter-spike (Wave 1, prove-or-kill), D2 indexer (tree-sitter floor + SCIP upgrade + edge extraction), D3 freshness (content-hash + one-hop re-validation), D4 query-CLI (deterministic, no-grep-fallback, fail-loud), D5 `/scan` consumer wiring.
- **Wave count:** 3 serial gates (Wave 1 kill-criteria → Wave 2 build → Wave 3 wiring). Wave 1 is a HARD gate.
- **Parallel-domain count:** within Wave 2, D2/D3/D4 are largely file-disjoint — partition validates with `gsd-t parallel --dry-run`.
- **Token-spend range:** defer to plan (no trailing-3 graph-milestone comparable; M20–M21 predates the token-log).
- **Open plan-phase decisions:** (1) the specific store (resolved by K1); (2) tree-sitter parallelism strategy if K2 is tight; (3) the edge-extraction taxonomy (salvaged-as-lessons from `graph-parsers.js`, built fresh on tree-sitter).
- **DEFER partition/plan** — this is a DEFINE-only milestone.

### M93 — definition retained below for reference — DEFINED 2026-06-23 12:47 PDT

**Problem (user, repeatedly, finally pinned 2026-06-23):** GSD-T replies are exhausting to read — too much preamble, process-narration, and unglossed jargon. The user misses real decisions (e.g. a contract item they don't remember agreeing to) because they're buried in volume. **Root cause: conciseness is a PROSE preference (it's even in the user's global CLAUDE.md: "No process narration. Ever.") and prose rules get ignored — proven live this session (I narrated intent before answering a pure question, violating my own rule).** GSD-T only reliably obeys DETERMINISTIC GATES. So the fix is a gate, not another instruction.

**The user's exact spec (verbatim intent):**
- **Question (wants an answer)** → answer FIRST, no preamble. No process-narration ("let me find X before I answer"). The answer the user later approved as the target FORMAT: answer-first, bullets, every code/jargon term glossed in plain language on FIRST use, expand only on request.
- **Action (about to change code)** → state intent FIRST (so the user can short-circuit a wrong direction). KEEP this — it's wanted and already works.
- **Discriminator:** am I about to modify something, or just tell something? Modify → announce intent. Tell → just tell.
- **Jargon rule:** never write a bare `S2-M7` / `HC-003` / acronym — gloss it (`S2-M7 (the milestone that added X)`, spell out the acronym) on first use.
- The dated banner (`[Jun 23 … — v…]`) STAYS — that's not the preamble being objected to.

**Build (gate + supporting instruction, BLOCK-conservative per user):**
- **D1 brevity-guard Stop hook** (`scripts/gsd-t-brevity-guard.js`) — fires on Stop, reads the last assistant message from `transcript_path` (reusing the `gsd-t-conversation-capture.js` tail-scan precedent), classifies the turn ANSWER-mode vs ACTION-mode (action = the turn contained Write/Edit/tool-mutation calls → allow intent-first; pure-text reply → ANSWER-mode, enforce). In answer-mode, BLOCK (decision:block / exit 2, date-guard precedent, FAIL-OPEN on error) when it detects egregious answer-mode preamble: ≥2 process-narration sentences before the first substantive answer, OR a bare unglossed jargon token from a known set. **Tuned CONSERVATIVE** — catch the egregious cases, never police every word (a false-block is its own friction).
- **D2 Reader Contract** — the sharpened question-vs-action + gloss-jargon rule baked into `templates/CLAUDE-global.md` (so it propagates) + the subagent prompts (`templates/prompts/*`, `templates/stacks/_*`), so the DEFAULT improves and the hook is the backstop.
- **D3 jargon-gloss commit lint** — a deterministic check for WRITTEN artifacts (briefs, progress entries, contracts): flag an unglossed `S2-M7`/`HC-003`/acronym at commit (the file surface the Stop hook can't reach).

**Scope:** GSD-T framework repo + propagate to ALL registered projects (fixes BinVoice verbosity too). **Out of scope:** removing/shrinking the dated banner (user keeps it).

**Falsifiable:** the Stop hook BLOCKS a seeded answer-mode reply that opens with 3 narration sentences; ALLOWS an action-mode reply that states intent before a code edit; ALLOWS the user-approved answer-first format; the jargon lint FAILS a doc with a bare `HC-003` and PASSES the glossed form. After propagation, BinVoice inherits the guard.

**Next:** partition into the 3 domains (D1 hook / D2 instruction / D3 lint — file-disjoint), execute, verify, complete.

### M92 — Understand-Before-Build (definition retained below for reference) — DEFINED 2026-06-23 10:59 PDT

**The cheap, high-leverage, no-graph half of backlog #44** (the BinVoice over-scoping fix). Promoted as #44a per the brief's review-recommended split; the graph half (#44b) is a SEPARATE later milestone, GATED on M92 moving the needle. Brief: `.gsd-t/design-briefs/understand-before-build-subtract-half.md` (read §0.5 first).

**Thesis:** GSD-T is a purely ADDITIVE gate pipeline — when a plan starts too high, every gate makes it bigger. M92 installs the missing *understand-first* + *prefer-smallest* + *reward-smaller* reflexes WITHOUT a code graph (grep-grounded), reusing shipped machinery. Goal is one event three ways: simpler · faster · smarter; the headline is **faster** — kill the BinVoice 4-cycle re-plan spiral.

**Three moves (each re-grounded on disk 2026-06-23):**
- **Move 1 — scope-assumption reflex (give M90's §2 trigger its response).** `bin/gsd-t-architectural-trigger.cjs` (M90 §2, R-ARCH-2) already FIRES on the BinVoice moment (a task whose `**Touches**` lists an existing file) and already has a `resolveResponseMode({spikeFeasible, spikePassed})` interface — but **the PRODUCER that decides feasibility is the stub** (backlog #42; `spikeFeasible` defaults true → spike-first). M92 adds the producer + reframes the ladder to **look → smallest → spike → defer** (grep-grounded "look," modeled on M90's SHIPPED §1 `research-gate.cjs` classify→grep→ground pipeline — NOT a new ladder, NOT M89 [retired into M90]). So the response is "classify scope-claim → grep what exists → propose smallest-altitude change," not "spike first."
- **Move 2 — verdict vocabulary keystone (+ deterministic shrink-metric).** `verify.workflow.js:206` freezes `overallVerdict` to a 3-enum where the only non-fail tokens are `VERIFIED`/`VERIFIED-WITH-WARNINGS`; `VERIFIED` = pure AND of additive gates — **the schema cannot SAY "we made it smaller."** M92 adds a first-class "smaller/leaner" success signal, fed by a DETERMINISTIC shrink-metric (net LOC / file-count / removed-vs-added from a `git diff --stat` envelope — measured, per [[feedback_measure_dont_claim]], NOT an LLM self-attesting "simpler"). One enum + one synthesis rule + one diff-stat input.
- **Move 3 — invert the default.** Today minimality is ONE prose line (`gsd-t-quick.workflow.js:186` "SIMPLICITY ABOVE ALL") with no teeth; ceremony (plan→execute, partition, competition) is the "Recommended" default. M92 flips it: prompts recommend the SMALLEST option; ceremony becomes opt-in, justified by the crux. (BinVoice recommended the heaviest option every turn; the user had to drag it down — autonomous runs have no one to drag.)

**Out of scope (explicitly — the brief's anti-over-scope discipline applied to M92 itself):** NO code graph (that's #44b, gated on M92). NO consolidation/N≥3 track (needs the graph). NO new standing subsystem — all three moves are insertions/reframes of shipped machinery (~10 files total est.). The shrink is a per-phase BEAT in spirit but M92 ships it as the verdict-metric + the reflex; full every-phase shrink-beat wiring can stage in if cheap, else defer.

**Falsifiable success:** re-run the BinVoice URL-change scenario (or a seeded fixture of it) → M92's reflex proposes the 1-file change, not the 36-file refactor; the verdict can emit "smaller" on a net-negative diff; the milestone/quick default no longer recommends the heaviest option. Headline metric: re-plan-cycle count / wall-clock-to-VERIFIED on the fixture drops vs. the pre-M92 baseline.

**Next:** partition into file-disjoint domains (likely 3 — one per move, the verify-spine move and the prompt move are file-disjoint; move 1 touches `architectural-trigger.cjs` + its workflow wiring). PAUSED here for user go (paradigm milestone touching the verify spine — deliberate launch, not auto-roll).

- **D2 `traceability-section-coverage`** (Wave 2) — section-citation grammar; tasks TRACE to PseudoCode sections; a section with no task = coverage gap (extends M83 traceability-gate).
- **D3 `milestone-two-altitude-flow`** (Wave 2) — two-altitude FLOW (high-level approach → detailed `PseudoCode-[Title].md`) + keep-or-supersede PROMPT, prose/protocol (the deterministic sign-off GATE moved to M88/Wave 3).
- **D4 `template-docripple-contract`** (Wave 2) — `templates/PseudoCode-spec.md` mold + doc-ripple membership (Living Documents table, Pre-Commit Gate, doc-ripple lint) + contract ownership.

**Wave 3 — M88 deterministic gates (4, to be partitioned now; each attaches to a Wave-1/2 deliverable):**
- **G1 sign-off state** — a code-readable "DEFINED" marker + `isDefined(milestone)` predicate (no milestone-state artifact exists today; unsigned detailed doc → NOT-DEFINED; signing flips it; skip = logged decision). Attaches to D3's flow.
- **G2 build→map derivation seam** — mechanical `build evidence → {rules:{<id>:{backedBy,contradicted}}}` derivation + end-to-end test (real build → derive → D1 gate). Closes the gap D1's map-only doctoring leaves.
- **G3 triad-consumption seam-check** — deterministic assert that `qa-subagent.md` / `red-team-subagent.md` carry the rule-set-ingest directive + unit test feeding guard-map JSON through the consumer, asserting RULE-IDs surface. Attaches to D1 + the triad.
- **G4 divergence-grammar round-trip** — `parseDivergence()`/`formatDivergence()` over the `⚠ Divergence:` flag (contract §4); byte-stable round-trip; malformed FAILS; count = checkable artifact. Attaches to D3's keep-or-supersede.

**Deterministic-gate bar (M87 sets it, M88 must meet it):** pass/fail is deterministic code, ZERO LLM judgment, structural-not-substring, proven by a killing test against byte-verbatim fixtures, no silent degradation. Memory: [[feedback_intention_first_pseudocode]], [[feedback_coverage_check_structural_not_substring]], [[feedback_no_silent_degradation]].

**Next action:** partition M88's 4 gates into Wave-3 domains, then execute Wave 1 (D1 kill gate) → Wave 2 (D2/D3/D4 parallel) → Wave 3 (G1-G4) → verify → complete-milestone.

### M84 — Auto-Competition (workflow self-decides whether to run a competition) — **COMPLETED at v4.3.10 (2026-06-05 20:42 PDT)**

**Status: COMPLETED — VERIFIED.** Single domain (auto-competition probe + opt-in→automatic conversion), built in-session. Origin: user, watching M82 competition stay opt-in: *"I do not want this to be opt-in. I want the workflow to determine when it's optimal to create a competition — three producers with a judge."* And the economic case (user): a better artifact produced upstream makes every downstream phase (pre-mortem, execute, verify) cheaper + more likely to pass first time, so the expected savings exceed the ~3× upstream cost — opt-in just means forgetting to use the thing that lowers total cost.

**Built.** Converted M82 competition from opt-in (`--competition N`) to AUTOMATIC in `templates/workflows/gsd-t-phase.workflow.js`: a **solution-space probe** runs at the start of each eligible phase (partition/milestone/discuss/design-decompose), after brief, before producing, and self-decides compete (3 producers + judge) vs single-draft. (a) **Probe on OPUS, not haiku** — deciding "≥2 genuinely different viable approaches?" is high-level reasoning that gates the whole 3× competition; a weak probe forfeits the feature (user caught this: *"Is Haiku smart enough to make this a judgment?"* — no). (b) **Biased toward competing** — uncertain → compete; probe failure → compete (fail-toward-options). (c) **Partition**: opus probe makes the pre-produce compete/skip call, the objective file-disjointness oracle still JUDGES the candidates. (d) **Phase-aware producer angles** (`ANGLES_BY_PHASE`) so a discuss/milestone/design producer isn't handed a partition-framed directive (Red Team MEDIUM). (e) **Overrides** (rarely needed): `competition: N` (2-5) force N, `competition: 0`/`noCompetition` force off, unset = auto; unparseable override warns + falls back to auto. (f) `meta.phases` now declares all 7 stages (also fixes the M83 cosmetic Plan-Hardening omission).

**Verification (real-sandbox + triad).**
- **Real-sandbox probe proof:** the opus probe ran through the actual Workflow sandbox and discriminated correctly — WIDE scenario (real-time collaborative editor, multiple architectures) → **compete=true, 3 approaches named** (CRDT-vs-OT / sync-authority / deployment-topology); NARROW scenario (bump copyright year, one file) → **compete=false** (*"exactly one correct outcome"*). Validates the user's instinct: the probe needs Opus-level reasoning, and it discriminates rather than blanket-competing.
- **Red Team (adversarial Workflow, Opus, fresh context): GRUDGING-PASS** — no CRITICAL/HIGH. Verified clean: state-wiring (let-decls set before consumers, no read-before-set), override logic (force-off/force-N/clamp/unset-→-probe all correct), eligibility (plan/impact/prd/doc-ripple/execute can NEVER compete), probe-failure (fail-toward-compete, can't crash/loop), cost-bound (1 probe + ≤5 producers + ≤2 judge + finalize + revalidate, no runaway), runtime-native, and no plan-hardening regression. Fixed the 1 MEDIUM (phase-aware angles — the latent M82 defect that now mattered because competition is the default path) + 3 LOWs (misleading partition-oracle comment, unparseable-arg warning, empty "Phase" stage on the competition path).
- **QA:** suite **1372 pass / 0 fail / 4 skip**; M71 runtime-native lint passes.

**Domain table:**

| Domain | Status | Tasks | Completed |
|--------|--------|-------|-----------|
| m84-auto-competition | verified | — | — |

**Versioning:** minor bump 4.2.10 → 4.3.10 (changed behavior — competition now automatic; additive overrides). Contract `competition-mode-contract.md` → v2.0.0. Tagged v4.3.10.

### M83 — Left-Shifted Plan Hardening (acceptance-traceability gate + adversarial pre-mortem) — **COMPLETED at v4.2.10 (2026-06-05 19:29 PDT)**

**Status: COMPLETED — VERIFIED.** 2 file-disjoint domains (D1 deterministic traceability gate · D2 adversarial pre-mortem protocol + plan-workflow wiring), built in-session. Origin: review of the NiceNote 9-milestone build, where the triad caught real bugs but LATE — M5's headline capability (100MB+ chunked read) shipped as DEAD CODE and burned 4 verify cycles. User's diagnosis: the failure is upstream in plan/scope; user's proposal: an adversarial risk-assessment agent at plan time. This milestone left-shifts failure detection from verify to plan.

**Goal (delivered).** Two blocking gates in the `plan` phase, run after the plan agent writes tasks.md and BEFORE execute: (1) deterministic **acceptance-traceability gate** — every behavioral task binds its ACs to a code path + a killing test; the headline must be impl+test; (2) adversarial **pre-mortem** — opus, fresh-context, predicts edge-case/dead-deliverable/NFR failures, each → a required test. The temporal dual of the Red Team (attack the design at plan, not just code at verify). The pre-mortem makes the post-mortem cheap.

**Built.** (a) `bin/gsd-t-traceability-gate.cjs` — parses `.gsd-t/domains/*/tasks.md`, emits `{ok,exitCode,violations}`; exit 4 blocks execute. Emphasis-stripped + colon-agnostic field detection; AC-anchored task detection (descriptive headings not dropped); test-check tied to Test/Files/AC fields; pytest conventions preserved; zero deps, never throws, pure. Dispatched as `gsd-t traceability-gate`; project + global bin tools. (b) `templates/prompts/pre-mortem-subagent.md` — the adversarial PLAN protocol (verdict BLOCK/CLEARED; every finding → a requiredTest; advisory notes forbidden). (f) doc-ripple: gsd-t-plan.md, README, gsd-t-help, CLAUDE-global (+ live ~/.claude/CLAUDE.md), project CLAUDE.md (protocols + brains lists), package.json minor bump.

All 5 fixed (emphasis-strip + colon-agnostic regexes, AC-anchored parsing, field-tied test check, fail-closed gate).
- **Re-validation Red Team:** all 5 confirmed fixed — but found a **regression the CRITICAL fix introduced** (underscore-stripping in `_bare` broke pytest `test_*.py`/`*_test.py` paths → false-FAIL valid Python plans, HIGH). Fixed via `_barePath`/`fieldValueRaw` (preserve underscores for value-level scans, strip emphasis only for label detection).

### M82 — Competition Mode (generate-and-judge for upstream wide-solution-space phases) — **COMPLETED at v4.1.10 (2026-06-05 17:49 PDT)**

**Status: COMPLETED — VERIFIED.** 2 file-disjoint domains (D1 judge engine + workflow arm · D2 contract + flags + doc-ripple), built in-session. Origin: brainstorm 2026-06-05 grounded in 2 deep-research runs (tasks `wkcnmqw8u` best-of-N/judge/debate + `wt4z2eqcp` synthesis-vs-pick-one/MoA/Frankenstein). Full spec in `.gsd-t/backlog.md` #26.

**Goal (delivered).** Opt-in `competition: N` on **upstream, pre-contract, wide-solution-space phases** (partition / milestone / discuss / design-decompose): fan out N parallel candidate-producers → a **judge stage** → winner. The *generative dual* of the orthogonal validation triad (adversarial). **Watershed rule: generate-and-judge ABOVE the contract; attack-and-filter BELOW it.** Never touches execute/plan/verify/integrate.

**Evidence base (citable, verified).** Best-of-N coverage scales log-linearly but is **judge-bounded** (Brown et al. arXiv 2407.21787; 3-vote) ⇒ the judge IS the feature. Synthesis beats pick-one on loosely-coupled tasks (MoA arXiv 2406.04692; 3-0) but NOT unconditionally (Frankenstein real). Frankenstein mechanism = candidate quality variance; **Self-MoA > Mixed-MoA** (arXiv 2502.00674; 3-0) ⇒ N samples of one strong model. Debate doesn't beat sampling+judge ⇒ skip it. Optimal N<10 ⇒ default off, cap 5.

**Built.** (a) `bin/gsd-t-competition-judge.cjs` — the selection oracle: `--kind partition` (objective, scores candidate decompositions via the SAME `bin/gsd-t-file-disjointness.cjs` oracle the dispatcher uses — a calculator, not an LLM critic; touch-path normalization) + `--kind generic` (deterministic rubric selector). Zero deps, never throws, pure. Dispatched as `gsd-t competition-judge`; added to project + global bin tools. (b) `templates/workflows/gsd-t-phase.workflow.js` — the competition arm: `competition: N` (clamp 2–5, default off) on eligible phases → `parallel()` of N Self-MoA producers (one strong model, prompt-angle diversity) → judge stage → finalizer (pick-one-at-thesis + union-at-line-item) → partition re-validates the graft and BLOCKS on a reintroduced overlap. Runtime-native (M71 lint passes). (c) `.gsd-t/contracts/competition-mode-contract.md` v1.0.0 STABLE (6 invariants). (d) `--competition N` flag + docs on `gsd-t-partition.md` / `gsd-t-milestone.md` / `gsd-t-design-decompose.md`. (e) doc-ripple: README, gsd-t-help, CLAUDE-global (+ live `~/.claude/CLAUDE.md`), project CLAUDE.md, package.json minor bump.

**Verification (orthogonal triad + measured SCs).**
- **SC#1 (headline, MEASURED on M82's own partition):** competition with 3 candidate partitions → winner `B-by-layer` with **3 parallel groups** (judge-engine ∥ workflow-arm ∥ contract-and-flags, file-disjoint) vs the **N=1 baseline's 1** parallel group → **3× measured parallelism**, strictly better. The deliberately-overlapping candidate (`C-overlap-trap`, shared `bin/gsd-t.js`) was correctly **disqualified** (`valid:false`) — a naive "more domains = better" judge would have picked it.
- **SC#2 (no Frankenstein):** invalid candidates never selected (HIGH-1 fix: all-invalid → hard-fail, not `candidates[0]`); finalized partition re-validated via the oracle, blocks on salvage overlap (HIGH-2 fix).
- **SC#3 (position-bias):** objective judge order-invariant (100%, reverse-order probe → same winner).
- **SC#4 (cost):** bounded by construction (N producers + judge + finalizer, no loops).
- **Red Team (adversarial Workflow, Opus, fresh context):** FAILed first pass — 3 HIGH (invalid-partition fallback to candidates[0]; finalizer never re-validated; subjective judge claimed-but-not-shuffled) + 2 MEDIUM (judge() threw on null candidate; unquoted projectDir + unescaped backticks). All 5 fixed; **re-validation Red Team GRUDGING-PASS** (all confirmed fixed by reading logic + executing scenarios, no new HIGH/CRITICAL). 2 LOW from recheck also closed (finalizedDomains now schema-required + absence blocks; tiebreak wording corrected). Re-confirms the orthogonal-validation contract: a fresh-context Workflow Red Team caught what the in-context build missed.
- **QA:** suite **1357 pass / 0 fail / 4 skip** (+6 M82 tests); M71 runtime-native lint passes; **real-sandbox acceptance gate passed** (judge integration ran end-to-end in the actual Workflow sandbox — proof v2: via=local, winner=B-by-layer, pass=true; the v1 proof caught a real envelope-propagation bug that lint+node --check could not, then fixed).

**Domain table:**

| Domain | Status | Tasks | Completed |
|--------|--------|-------|-----------|
| m82-d1-competition-arm-and-judge | verified | — | — |
| m82-d2-contract-flags-docripple | verified | — | — |

- NEW `templates/workflows/gsd-t-scan.workflow.js`: (a) **volume-probe** stage (haiku) counts files/routes/tables/components per top-level area → derives a **slice list** (e.g. each of `src/lib/`'s 24 subdirs = 1 slice; ~15–25 slices for Hilo, 1 for a tiny repo); (b) `pipeline()` per-slice **deep finder** (dimension-aware, mandate "enumerate every module, do NOT sample") → **single verify pass** per finding (user choice 2026-05-29: single verify, not 3-vote) confirming against real code, killing false positives; (c) `budget`-aware slice depth; (d) **synthesis** stage (opus) dedup/merge into `techdebt.md`, re-rank critical→low, continue TD numbering from archive. **Origin**: m61-deferred. M61 ported the orchestration core to native Workflow scripts (`templates/workflows/*.workflow.js`) but deferred deleting the old M40/M44 orchestration shell those scripts replace. M65 retires that shell.

**Goal**: Delete the obsolete orchestration shell + untangle `headless-exit-codes.cjs` from the CLI so it too can go, with zero dangling references and no new test failures beyond the M61 carryover baseline.

**Scope (REVISED from the raw brief after live reference scan — user-approved 2026-05-29):**

The raw brief named `gsd-t-parallel.cjs`, `parallel-cli.cjs`, `parallel-cli-tee.cjs` for deletion. **Live scan proved these are M61 KEEP-list substrate, NOT retireable shell** — they are load-bearing:
- `bin/gsd-t-verify-gate.cjs:31` requires `parallel-cli.cjs::runParallel` (the orthogonal-validation Track-2 engine).
- `templates/workflows/_lib.js:107` shells to `gsd-t-parallel.cjs` for `proveFileDisjointness()` (the new Workflow layer runs ON it).
- `parallel-cli-tee.cjs` is required by `parallel-cli.cjs`.

Deleting them would break the migrated Workflows + verify triad. **User decision (2026-05-29): delete only the true shell; KEEP all three.**

**IN (delete) — 8 files, 1,838 bin/ LOC:**
- `bin/gsd-t-orchestrator.js` (543) + `-worker.cjs` (228) + `-queue.cjs` (180) + `-config.cjs` (161) — the M40 external orchestrator, now superseded by `gsd-t-execute.workflow.js`.

- `bin/headless-exit-codes.cjs` (67) — inline `mapHeadlessExitCode` into `bin/gsd-t.js` (its only remaining requirer; the supervisor that justified its separate-file decoupling was deleted in M61 D2), then delete the file.

**ALSO clean (references + dispatch + tests + hooks):**

Resolving that (wire it back or retire it) is a separate design-pipeline decision, flagged as backlog, NOT bundled into this orchestration-shell retirement.

### M61 — Platform Reconciliation (Native-First GSD-T) — **PARTITIONED** (2026-05-29 11:46 PDT)

**Status: PARTITIONED — 8 domains scoped under `.gsd-t/domains/m61-d{1-8}-*/`; `m61-integration-points.md` written; Wave 0 (v3.x-legacy branch) already DONE. Awaiting `/gsd-t-plan`. Baseline locked: bin/ = 37,785 LOC / 109 files at v3.29.11 (SC1 target ≤12,000 LOC).**

**Origin**: Opus 4.8 + current Claude Code (native 1M context, native background **Workflows** with deterministic pipeline/parallel/barriers/schema-validation/budget, native parallel agents, `/context`, `/usage`, Skills, comprehensive hooks, `/code-review ultra`) have absorbed the entire infrastructure layer GSD-T built across M34–M54 to compensate for a 200K window + a runtime that couldn't spawn/background/relay. A maximal-native Workflow bake-off (2026-05-29) re-ran M58 as **one Workflow script** and reproduced every deterministic gate + both domains exactly — AND its adversarial Red Team caught a live CRITICAL (→ M60) that M58's in-context review missed. **Conclusion: the orchestration migration is both safe and strictly more reliable.**

**Goal**: Collapse GSD-T to its irreplaceable methodology layer riding on native primitives. Target: bin/ from ~38K LOC → ~8K LOC. **Net objective: most efficient, reliable, predictable build/rebuild/debug/deliver process** — which means *less custom infra to maintain*, not more.

**Domains (pre-partition shape — finalized at partition):**

- **D1 retire-context-runway** — delete the context-meter / runway machinery now obsoleted by native 1M context + `/context` + native compaction: `token-budget.cjs`, `context-meter-config.cjs(+test)`, `context-budget-audit.cjs`, `runway-estimator.cjs`, `model-windows.cjs(+test)`, the context-meter PostToolUse hook, `.context-meter-state.json` plumbing. (~1,580 LOC + hook.)
- **D2 retire-unattended-relay** — delete the cross-session relay supervisor now replaced by native background Workflows + `/loop`: `gsd-t-unattended.cjs(+.js dup)`, `-safety.cjs(+.js)`, `-platform.cjs(+.js)`, `-heartbeat.cjs`, `supervisor-pid-fingerprint.cjs`, `handoff-lock.cjs(+.js)`, `headless-auto-spawn.cjs(+.js)`, `check-headless-sessions.js`, `unattended-watch-format.cjs`, `gsd-t-worker-dispatch.cjs`, `gsd-t-orchestrator-recover.cjs` + the 3 `gsd-t-unattended*` commands. (~8,800 LOC — largest demolition.)
- **D3 retire-token-telemetry** — delete the capture/attribution loop M38 already admitted "never produced action," now covered by native `/usage`: `gsd-t-token-capture.cjs` (+ the MANDATORY-wrapper rule in CLAUDE files), `-token-dashboard/-backfill/-regenerate-log/-report-tokens`, `-tool-attribution`, `-tool-cost`, `-in-session-usage`, `-economics`, `metrics-collector/-rollup`, `gsd-t-capture-lint.cjs`. (~4,100 LOC.)
- **D4 retire-viewer-dashboard** — delete the custom SSE viewer/dashboard now covered by native `/workflows` + Agent View: `live-activity-report.cjs`, `gsd-t-transcript-tee.cjs`, `gsd-t-stream-feed-client.cjs`, `parallelism-report.cjs`, `log-tail.cjs`, `watch-progress.js`, `event-stream.cjs` + `scripts/gsd-t-dashboard-server.js` + viewer HTML + conversation-capture hooks. (~2,000 LOC + scripts.)
- **D5 retire-proof-scratch** — delete one-time milestone-proof artifacts (0 references): `m44-proof-measure`, `m46-iter-proof`, `m46-worker-proof`, `m55-substrate-proof`, `gsd-t-benchmark-orchestrator`, `gsd-t-parallel-probe`, `gsd-t-ratelimit-probe(+worker)`. (~1,900 LOC.)
- **D6 migrate-orchestration-to-workflow** — port the orchestration core to native Workflow scripts: `gsd-t-orchestrator.js`, `orchestrator.js`, `-orchestrator-worker/-queue/-config`, `gsd-t-parallel.cjs`, `parallel-cli(+tee)`, `spawn-plan-*` → a small set of Workflow scripts. **KEEP the brains** (`gsd-t-file-disjointness.cjs` domain-boundary prover, `gsd-t-task-graph.cjs` reader) but RUN them inside Workflows. (~6,500 LOC → ~500.)
- **D7 keep-and-reframe-validation** — KEEP the methodology gates; reframe Red Team / QA / Design-Verify as **Workflow stages** (perspective-diverse adversarial `parallel()`), de-duped against native `/code-review ultra`. KEEP unchanged: `gsd-t-verify-gate(+judge)`, `gsd-t-ci-parity`, `gsd-t-build-coverage`, `gsd-t-test-data-ledger` (+ M60-hardened adapters), `journey-coverage(+cli)`, `cli-preflight`, `gsd-t-context-brief` (MORE valuable now — cheap context for Workflow agents), `playwright-bootstrap`/`ui-detection`, scan engine, `rule-engine`, `graph-*`, `archive-progress`, `global-sync-manager`.
- **D8 doc-ripple-and-cockpit** — rewrite CLAUDE-global/project + commands→Skills mapping to drop retired-infra rules; **bake in the desktop-as-cockpit outcome** (see SC7).

**Falsifiable Success Criteria:**
- **SC1** — bin/ LOC drops from ~38K to ≤ ~12K (measured `wc -l` before/after); every deleted file proven to have zero live references first (safety scan).
- **SC2** — a representative milestone (re-run of M58 or M52) completes end-to-end via the native-Workflow harness with all KEEP-list gates green and Red Team clean — i.e., the bake-off result reproduces after the demolition.
- **SC3** — zero regressions on the full unit suite vs. the M60 baseline (2466 pass / 1 known-flaky / 3 sqlite-skip), excluding tests deleted *with* their retired subject.
- **SC4** — `gsd-t doctor` passes with no dangling references to retired modules; no command file references a deleted `bin/` script.
- **SC5** — Red Team / QA / Design-Verify run as Workflow stages (not bespoke Task spawns), de-duped against `/code-review ultra` (no double-paying for correctness review).
- **SC6** — every retired capability has a named native replacement documented in the milestone archive (retire→native map), so nothing is lost silently (measure-don't-claim).
- **SC7 (desktop-as-cockpit)** — after M61, **no routine build / rebuild / debug / deliver action requires the user to hand-type in a terminal**; the desktop app can drive all of it (orchestrate via Bash + Workflows + Skills). Verified by walking the full loop (partition→plan→execute→verify→deliver) from the desktop on one real task. The only terminal-native residue allowed: background hooks (which run automatically, not user-initiated) and "must-outlive-app-close" overnight jobs.
- **SC8** — Red Team GRUDGING PASS on the reconciled framework (adversarial Workflow pass finds no CRITICAL/HIGH in the migrated orchestration).

**Sequencing note (user directive, 2026-05-29)**: M61 is **initiated from the terminal CLI** — it is the last big CLI-dependent job (editing/removing hooks, supervisor teardown, heavy git surgery on the very infra being removed). After M61 lands (SC7 verified), the user switches to the **desktop as single cockpit**.

**Pre-partition assessment**: large milestone — 8 domains, mostly file-disjoint (each retire-domain owns its own bin files), but D6 (migrate) and D7/D8 (keep/reframe/doc) have ordering dependencies (migrate orchestration before deleting old orchestration; reframe validation before doc-ripple). Likely 3–4 waves: retire-disjoint (D1∥D3∥D4∥D5) → migrate (D6) → reframe+retire-relay (D7∥D2) → doc+cockpit (D8). **Destructive Action Guard applies throughout** — every deletion domain runs a zero-live-reference safety scan and pauses for approval before removing working functionality. Discussion phase recommended (this reshapes the framework's identity).

### M58 — Test Data Cleanup Gate **COMPLETE** at v3.28.10 (2026-05-27). Origin: GSD-T-Board v0.1.10 ran `gsd-t-verify`, the Playwright suite passed, the milestone was tagged VERIFIED — and 2442 `E2E_TEST_*` / `E2E_DRAG_*` ideas stayed live in the production data store. Root cause: GSD-T had no convention for tracking test data inserted during Verify and no purge step after the suite completes. **D1 test-data-ledger**: `bin/gsd-t-test-data-ledger.cjs` ships `{appendInsert, listInserts, purgeRunInserts, registerAdapter}` against an append-only JSONL ledger at `.gsd-t/test-data-ledger.jsonl`; 3 built-in adapters under `bin/gsd-t-test-data-adapters/` (`localStorage-key-prefix`, `file-json-array`, `sqlite-table-where`) each enforce a tagged-prefix guard as defense in depth; CLI `gsd-t test-data --list|--purge --run <id>` (exit 0/4/64). **D2 verify-cleanup-step + tagging convention**: `templates/test-helpers/test-data-fixture.ts` ships the Playwright `withTestData()` fixture (composes `{PREFIX}_{runId}_{counter}` IDs, calls `appendInsert` on `register`, opt-in `purgePerTest`); `commands/gsd-t-verify.md` Step 4.5 runs `gsd-t test-data --purge` after E2E + before VERDICT, FAILs verify on adapter errors. **SCs**: 7/7 PASS — ledger records 5 inserts, purge removes them and reports `purged.length===5`, planted adapter throw lands in `errors[]` (FAIL decision), clean E2E reports `purged=5 skipped=0 errors=0`, **2649/2649 tests pass (zero regressions; baseline was 2587)**, Red Team **6/6 attacks defended** (untagged-id reject, tag-prefix-tamper reject, unknown-adapter structured error, SQL-injection reject, no stray writes, bad-adapter-return-value caught), doc-ripple complete. **Contracts**: `test-data-ledger-contract.md` v1.0.0 STABLE + `test-data-tagging-contract.md` v1.0.0 STABLE. **Versioning**: minor bump 3.27.10 → 3.28.10 (new feature, additive).

- 2026-06-30 06:34 PDT: [fix][v4.13.12] **Scan graph probe silently fell back to grep-mode despite a LIVE graph.** Found on a real NiceNote scan (#12): scan announced `GRAPH-FALLBACK — graph index not available` and ran grep-mode, but the graph was demonstrably live (156 files, compiler-accurate, all verbs + freshness verified working that same session). Root cause, PROVEN by reproducing the probe through a real haiku agent: scan's `runCli` (in `templates/workflows/gsd-t-scan.workflow.js`) told a **haiku** agent to "return ONLY the raw JSON line" then `JSON.parse`'d the free-text reply — haiku wrapped the JSON in a ```` ```json ```` markdown fence, `JSON.parse` threw, the catch returned `{ok:false,reason:"graph-unavailable"}`, scan demoted to grep-mode. CLI/graph/cwd/bin-presence all ruled out one-by-one before the live repro confirmed the fence. This is the deterministic-orchestration anti-pattern (a reliability-critical gate routed through an LLM's free text). Fix (mirrors the proven `gsd-t-verify.workflow.js` runCli): (1) schema-validated probe — `schema: _GRAPH_CLI_ENVELOPE_SCHEMA` → StructuredOutput returns structured JSON via the tool layer, never fenced prose (the real fix); (2) project-local bin → global `gsd-t graph` fallback (was hardcoded `node bin/...cjs`); (3) dropped `2>/dev/null`, surface `reason`/`via` in the fallback log. Probe stays `model:"haiku"` (mechanical call — schema not tier is what fixes it). Regression test added in `test/m94-d6-scan-consumer.test.js` (source-structural: runCli MUST use schema, MUST NOT JSON.parse(result…), MUST have global-bin fallback — the prior test only simulated recorded envelopes, never the parsing layer). Suite 2542/2546; M71 sandbox + M85 tier lints green. Class follow-on (NOT this fix): audit quick/debug/integrate/phase workflows for the same haiku-fence pattern. Files: `templates/workflows/gsd-t-scan.workflow.js`, `test/m94-d6-scan-consumer.test.js`, CHANGELOG.md, README.md, GSD-T-README.md, package.json (4.13.11→4.13.12), progress.md. Next: `/cpua` publish + propagate.

- 2026-06-29 13:36 PDT: [M98 SHIPPED at v4.13.10 — the graph serves code] **Built + verified the milestone that makes the graph SERVE CODE, not just index it.** 3 file-disjoint domains, 1 wave, single session. **D1** — extractor records each function/method/class END line (`node.endPosition`) onto a new `nodes.end_line` column (idempotent `ALTER TABLE` migration onto pre-M98 graphs; kept fresh by the existing DELETE+reinsert re-index). **D2** — `gsd-t graph body <funcId|symbol>` reads the live file, slices start..end, attaches imports + class header (methods) + caller list; ambiguous bare symbol → candidates (never a merged body); a pre-M98 null-end node is re-indexed inline (tier-preserving — never silently downgrades a compiler-accurate file to plain floor; labels STALE-SCIP). **D3** — PostToolUse `Read`-intercept hook (`scripts/gsd-t-read-intercept.js`): a structural read (offset/limit inside one known function) is AUGMENTED with a pointer to the precise `body` slice; default = pass-through (a bare/edit read is NEVER shrunk); fail-open; registered/removed by `gsd-t install`/uninstall. **Open implementation question resolved → option (c)** conservative pass-through (no-regression). **All 7 ACs green** incl. - 2026-06-29 13:03 PDT: [M98 DEFINED — researched, all decisions locked, paused for /clear] **Scoped the milestone that makes the graph SERVE CODE, not just index it.** Closes M97's deferred #6 (graph not consulted on Read). Today the graph is index-only (names/files/lines/edges, NO bodies — confirmed: `nodes` has no source column). M98: a `body` query verb returns a single function's source (sliced LIVE from disk by line range + class header + imports + callers), and a Read-intercept hook augments structural code-reads. **Research (2 threads, cited):** function-level granularity is unanimous (cAST/Sourcegraph/Aider/Greptile); Kythe/Glean store body+offsets but SCIP/Cody read live (always fresh); measured ~43× token win (one function ~180 tok vs whole file ~7,750). **6 decisions LOCKED with user:** (1) READ LIVE from disk, don't store bodies — local files only, benchmark showed read-live ~25µs vs db-blob ~5µs (both invisible), and freshness automation ALREADY re-indexes a stale file before answering (verified: parse_and_put does DELETE+re-insert nodes with fresh @line) so line ranges are current → zero stale risk, nothing to store/sync; (2) serve the relevant SLICE not whole file; (3) YES a `body` verb; (4) intercept Read only (not Glob/LS); (5) capture function END lines (only start is stored today — the one real schema/extractor change); (6) attach class header + imports + callers. **ONE open implementation question for partition (not a design decision):** how Read-intercept distinguishes a structural read (serve slice) from an edit-intent read (pass full file) — lean conservative (default pass-through, rely on the explicit `body` verb) for no-regression. Definition: [`.gsd-t/milestones/M98-DEFINITION-graph-serves-code-slices.md`](.gsd-t/milestones/M98-DEFINITION-graph-serves-code-slices.md). NEXT after /clear: `/gsd-t-partition` M98. - 2026-06-26 19:38 PDT: [M94][OOM FIX] **Fixed the real bug behind the Mac OOM-crash + a cross-domain signature mismatch.** Root cause was NOT a heavy test: `runFreshnessCheck(storePath)` in `bin/gsd-t-graph-query-cli.cjs` on a fake/non-existent store path derived `projectRoot = path.dirname(path.dirname(storePath))` = `"/"`, then `compute_touched_files(db, "/")` → `walkTree("/")` recursively read the ENTIRE filesystem → ballooned to ~17GB → OOM crashed the machine. Surfaced by `fault-6` in `test/m94-d5-fault-injection-fail-loud.test.js` (D4 module present → took the live branch with `/fake/store`). **Fix 1:** `runFreshnessCheck` now returns `{ok:false, reason:'graph-unavailable'}` when `openDb` finds no real store at the derived root — BEFORE any touched-set walk ([RULE] parser-fail-disables-loud-never-silent). **Fix 2 (defense-in-depth):** `walkTree` refuses to recurse when `path.resolve(dir)` equals the filesystem root or `os.homedir()` — fixture-safe (does NOT depend on `.gsd-t` existing, so `mkdtemp` D4 fixtures still work; a first attempt that guarded on `existsSync(<root>/.gsd-t)` broke 11 fixture tests and was reverted). **Fix 3 (cross-domain bug, same pass):** `freshness_check_on_query` called `parseAndPut(rel, absPath, db, projectRoot)` but D3's real `parse_and_put` signature is `(absPath, relPath, { db, scip })` (`bin/gsd-t-graph-index.cjs:250`) — in production this passed `rel` where `absPath` was expected and `db` arrived undefined, so re-indexing a stale file parsed the wrong path. FIX: `graph-indexer-build-contract.md` (D3-T2) FREEZES `parse_and_put`'s tier behavior as an invariant BEFORE D3/D4 execute — re-run SCIP for that language if feasible, OR honestly downgrade-with-flag `tier=tree-sitter-floor-STALE-SCIP` (new enum value in `graph-store-schema-contract.md` + the D5 query envelope), NEVER silently relabel plain `compiler-accurate` / plain `tree-sitter-floor` / drop to an unlabeled approximate edge. New test `test/m94-d3-tier-preserved-on-reindex.test.js` (D3-T5): build a SCIP-present fixture so a file is compiler-accurate, edit it, parse_and_put, assert re-upgraded OR explicitly STALE-SCIP-flagged; FAIL-LOUD-SKIP `scip-indexer-not-present` if no SCIP installed (`[RULE] reindex-tier-never-silently-downgraded`). **R4-3 (HIGH — who-calls function-identity ambiguity; not provable on real data):** `who-calls <function>` took a bare NAME, but real codebases have many same-named functions (handle/init/run/get/render) across files — `who-calls('handle')` on real Atos MERGES wrong callers; AC-2's hand-checked fixtures can pick unique names and pass while the query is broken on real data. FIX: define a `funcId = file#function` identity key (FQN / `file#function@line` where overloaded) in `graph-query-cli-contract.md` + `graph-store-schema-contract.md`; call edges keyed by `funcId` at BOTH ends (D3-T1 emits it); a bare name matching multiple `funcId`s returns `{ok:false, reason:"ambiguous-function", candidates:[...]}` or per-candidate grouped results, NEVER a flat merge. New test `test/m94-d5-who-calls-identity.test.js` (D5-T4): TWO foo's in different files with distinct callers; `who-calls('a.ts#foo')` returns ONLY a.ts's callers; bare `who-calls('foo')` disambiguates (`[RULE] who-calls-function-identity-disambiguated`). Until who-calls identity is defined+tested, AC-2 who-calls correctness is NOT provable on real data. **R4-4 (MEDIUM — multi-file freshness coherence):** the store's per-file atomicity covers ONE in-flight single-file write vs a read of THAT file. But `compute_touched_files()` returns the WHOLE-TREE dirty set — a branch-switch/git-pull/rebase dirties HUNDREDS of files re-indexed inline before answering, and per-file atomicity ≠ multi-file query coherence. FIX: `graph-freshness-contract.md` (D4-T1) declares the multi-file dirty-set re-index is SERIALIZED and the query observes the post-re-index COHERENT state (a who-imports(X) whose edges span several re-indexing files = all-new for EVERY contributor, never a mix). - 2026-06-25 16:56 PDT: [fix][gsd-t-phase.workflow.js runCli retry] During M94 define, the M90 stated-claims pipeline logged `classify failed: no envelope` on all 5 load-bearing external claims. ROOT CAUSE (not the claims, not the classifier): `runCli` delegates each CLI call to a haiku helper agent (not a subprocess), and a return can transiently come back missing its parsed result; the loose `_CLI_ENVELOPE_SCHEMA` (only `ok`+`exitCode` required, `envelope` untyped) lets a result-less return through, surfacing later as the cryptic "no envelope". Verified the classifier itself is healthy (`node bin/gsd-t-research-gate.cjs classify "..." --json` → exit 0, valid JSON). NOT a correctness hole (pipeline logs-and-continues; the claim FACTS were independently verified via the deep-research run minutes earlier) — a reliability bug in the helper layer that wraps EVERY workflow CLI call (preflight, verify-gate, etc.). FIX: `runCli` retries ONCE when JSON was expected but no parsed result returned (covers both the throw path via="error" AND the malformed-return path ok=false+absent-result); a real CLI failure that returned valid JSON (envelope present, ok=false) is NOT retried — true result, not a transient miss. Hardens every phase/wave/integrate/debug workflow before M94 Wave-1 spikes (K1/K2) lean on runCli for real Atos measurements. Edited repo source (propagates on next publish); `node --check` passes. Files: templates/workflows/gsd-t-phase.workflow.js (runCli), progress.md (this entry). NOTE: not yet published to the live installed package — runs from repo source.

- 2026-06-21 15:55 PDT: [m89][PAUSE + re-scope][backlog #38/#39] User paused M89 at verify (after 8 verify cycles, all converging on the silent-miss class) and RE-SCOPED. Two insights: (1) **M89 is too narrow.** Its "guessing" framing only covered FACTUAL assumptions ("do I know what the code/API says?"). The user named the dangerous omission: the system also assumes an APPROACH/architecture is correct without proof ("I'll fix it this way"; "the existing code was written right, build on it") and PLOWS FORWARD on the unproven approach — the root of binvoice's whack-a-mole + the M87 (7-cycle) and M89 (8-cycle) plan/verify loops (each cycle a new "right fix" on a wrong premise). The real feature = the UNPROVEN-ASSUMPTION doctrine: any unproven assumption (factual OR architectural) → STOP → research how others solved it → re-examine the premise → then proceed. Backlogged #38 (HIGHEST leverage; M89's external-fact auto-research becomes its factual slice). The trigger of the re-scope: M89's classifier recognized "external" via a hardcoded ~40-vendor list — a frozen belief for an OPEN set; any out-of-list vendor (GitHub/Slack/OpenAI) silently routed internal → the exact silent-miss M89 exists to prevent. Lesson: never hardcode a finite list for an open category; mechanical layer knows only CLOSED sets (own repo files), LLM judges the open world. (2) **Red Team has no realism/scope gate** — escalates unlikely/contrived edge cases to CRITICAL with equal weight to real money/security bugs. User's design (banked #39): a separate Realism agent the Red Team argues scope with (2 attempts, 2 rejections → documented deferred-out-of-scope); + my refinements: Realism rules only on scope-not-validity with a HARD FLOOR (money/security/data-loss/silent-wrong-output always in-scope), deferral-with-ledger not dismissal. - 2026-06-18 15:47 PDT: [m89][rethink][re-define] HALTED the plan loop at cycle-2 (2 CRITICALs) and rethought the premise WITH the user — the disposition was "halt and rethink", not patch-through. The cycle-2 pre-mortem proved the original framing OVERCLAIMED: a "fully deterministic trigger that REPLACES the LLM should-I-research discretion" is impossible because DETECTING you need info is itself a judgment (finding #2: gap-emission seam unowned; finding #1: A4 can't catch a gap never stated; finding #3: a proper-noun-less external gap defaults internal → silent false-negative). Same shape as M87 cycle-4 (a milestone held to a determinism bar part of it structurally can't meet). USER REFRAME (sharper + more enforceable): the trigger is NOT "did I notice a gap?" but **"for every load-bearing claim — KNOWN or GUESSING?"** A guess is a claim ON THE PAGE → inspectable (unlike an absent gap). Three guess-types: unknown / assumed (asserting a shape never verified — "I get a url back" because it makes sense) / stale (knew it, but external+time-varying+aged — was-true ≠ is-true; DEFAULT fail-toward-verify, don't trust the agent's self-staleness-assessment).
